Chris ibe
Wednesday, September 73, 2023 11:31 AM

Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission
Public Comment Re: SIC Agenda Item 3 - Sustainable Buildings Strategy

Sustainability & Infrastructure Commissioners,

| appreciate your leadership in the City of San Mateo's decarbonization efforts and the release

of the draft study for review. San Mateo's commitment to decarbonization is commendable.

| strongly support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the city's structures, primarily for

health and financial reasons:

Local Health Impacts: Gas appliances pose identified health risks. The Bay Area Air Quality
Management District recently passed Rule 9-4 and 9-6 to eliminate future gas water heaters
and HVAC systems due to the health effects of nitrogen oxide and particulate matter. The staff
report estimates doing so would save up to 85 lives and 15,000 asthma attacks a year. Note,

this is for outdoor air. Indoor air is likely worse.

Regional/Global Health Impacts: Burning natural gas/methane contributes to a warming
climate with adverse effects on residents’ lives, from extreme heat to more destructive
wildfires. Extreme heat is the leading weather cause of death. Climate change multiplies these

threats.

Environmental Concerns: Methane gas extraction methods like hydraulic fracturing harm our

environment and frontline communities.

Cost Savings: Transitioning to electric will bring long-term cost savings, benefiting households

by an estimated $1,800 annually. As technologies advance, costs will further decrease.

Local Support: San Mateo benefits from local initiatives and incentives, making electrification

affordable and accessible.

Simplified Electrification: The grid is becoming more reliable, and new electric products reduce
the need for extensive rewiring. Streamlined processes and local workforce development

support electrification.

230 of 332


--- page 231 ---
Denying the urgency of decarbonization ignores the reality of an unhealthy, hotter, costlier,
and less predictable future. Decarbonization aligns with both moral and financial
considerations. With numerous compelling reasons to accelerate electrification in San Mateo,

| urge you to continue facilitating our progress.
Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to public welfare.

Sincerely,

Chris Gilbert

and other mental health issues because of uncertainty caused by the ongoing environmental crisis, | appreciate your
leadership in the City of San Mateo's decarbonization efforts and the release of the draft study for review. San Mateo's
commitment to decarbonization is commendable.

| strongly support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the city's structures, primarily for health and financial reasons
as outlined below:

¢ Local Health Impacts: Gas appliances pose identified health risks. The Bay Area Air Quality Management District
recently passed Rule 9-4 and 9-6 to eliminate future gas water heaters and HVAC systems due to the health
effects of nitrogen oxide and particulate matter. The staff report estimates doing so would save up to 85 lives
and 15,000 asthma attacks a year. Note, this is for outdoor air. Indoor air is likely worse.

* Regional/Global Health Impacts: Burning natural gas/methane contributes to a warming climate with adverse
effects on residents’ lives, from extreme heat to more destructive wildfires. Extreme heat is the leading weather
cause of death. Climate change multiplies these threats.

* Environmental Concerns: Methane gas extraction methods like hydraulic fracturing harm our environment and
frontline communities.

* Cost Savings: Transitioning to electric will bring long-term cost savings, benefiting households by an estimated
$1,800 annually. As technologies advance, costs will further decrease.

* Local Support: San Mateo benefits from local initiatives and incentives, making electrification affordable and
accessible.

* Simplified Electrification: The grid is becoming more reliable every day, and new electric products reduce the
need for extensive rewiring. Peninsula Clean Energy is streamlining processes and developing a one-stop shop to
assist homeowners with electrification (whole-home and partial). Community groups are working with unions
and contractors to develop the electrification workforce,

From: Michelle 0)
Sent: Wednesday, September 13, 2023 1:08 PM

To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission
Subject: Support for San Mateo Building Decarbonization

Dear Sustainability & Infrastructure Commissioners,

| am a longtime resident of San Mateo, and a mother of two who is deeply concerned about the climate crisis,
and its ever-worsening impacts on the health, safety and economic vitality of our wonderful San Mateo
community.

| am grateful for the City's leadership in implementing its important decarbonization objectives and for releasing
the draft study of building decarbonization for review. At this time, | would like to urge you to continue the
forward momentum on this process. We need to keep supporting decarbonization —through all means
possible, but specifically, by focusing on building electrification.

| support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the City’s structures for the following reasons:

1) Climate: The warming climate, which is directly related to emissions of natural gas/methane, will have
damaging effects on the lives and livelihoods of community members. We have seen that impacts include
everything from extreme heat (which is dangerous to children, the elderly, and the significant number of
residents who lack air conditioning), fiercer and wetter storms, and more frequent and more destructive
wildfires. These are crises that interact and overlap since climate change is a threat multiplier.

2) Environmental: The methane gas we burn comes from dangerous practices such as hydraulic fracturing
that pollute the water and air and imperil frontline communities.

3) Health & Safety: Burning methane in our homes here in San Mateo is an unsafe practice with many
identified health risks, for instance, from gas stoves. These negative impacts are especially harmful to
children.

4) Cost Savings: Switching to electric will reduce costs in the long run (and far sooner when including
incentives). Rewiring America's electrification guide estimates "Households will save on average $1,800 a year
by going electric". As technologies begin to scale, the costs will drop further. NREL reported in a recent model /
study that "Higher levels of electrification with rapid advancements in the cost and performance of end-use
electric technologies can result in net energy system savings—up to $800 billion in the high electrification

scenario." Moreover, a wide variety of existing Peninsula Clean Energy rebates, newer tax credits created by
the Inflation Reduction Act, and other available funding makes electrification more affordable (as the Rincon

report indicates: “Whole home electrification could be less expensive for building owners in San Mateo than
replacing appliances with gas, once rebates are included").

6) Ease of Transition: Electrification is getting easier for residents, and will continue to do so. The grid is
getting more reliable all the time. New electric appliances/products have been coming onto the market that will
strain the grid less, and significantly minimize the necessity for rewiring work and service upgrades. PCE, the
IRA, and the state are creating streamline permit processes. PCE is developing a one-stop shop to assist
homeowners with their electrification retrofits. Local organizations are working with local unions and
contractors to develop the electrification workforce. This is no longer the same era that it was for the early
“home electrifiers.” This forward momentum will only continue.

237 of 332


--- page 238 ---
Those who oppose decarbonization and want to choose business as usual are merely in denial that the future
is already getting hotter, more expensive, less predictable, and more deadly. Furthermore, the City has hired a
very capable consultant, Rincon, to thoroughly analyze all issues, considerations, opportunities, etc. with
respect to the City’s decarbonization planning. The report being presented to the Commission tonight has set
forth a thoughtful timeframe for this process, which includes planned community outreach. | respectfully
request that the Commissioners trust and follow this process, and ask questions and provide input on
what is presented to the SIC on the consultant’s timeline, rather than revisiting opponents’ objections on
topics that are out of step with the consultant’s timeline and appear to be aimed at fear mongering.

Decarbonization is the better choice both from a moral and financial standpoint. With so many common-sense
reasons to accelerate electrification in San Mateo, | am hopeful that you will continue to facilitate our progress
on this issue. | look forward to participating in the community engagement process for the City's
decarbonization planning as it unfolds.

Thank you,
Michelle Hudson

San Mateo

From: Julie oe
Sent: Wednesday, September 13, 2023 1:30 PM

To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Cc: Robert Gould; Jeffrey Mann; robertwhitehair2@gmail.com

Subject: For 9/13/23 Commission Meeting: Comments re: Establish policies to decarbonize and
electrify existing buildings and eliminate natural gas use by 2030

Attachments: 091323 San Mateo Electrify.pdf

For 9/13 Commission Meeting: Comments re: Establish policies to decarbonize and electrify existing buildings and
eliminate natural gas use by 2030

Sent on behalf of San Francisco Bay Physicians for Social Responsibility
Please see below and attached.

September 11, 2023
Dear San Mateo Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission,

| represent San Francisco Bay Physicians for Social Responsibility (SF Bay PSR), a group of thousands of health
professionals and advocates in the Bay Area who seek to protect the health of our patients and communities
who are threatened by the climate emergency that is destroying our life support system. SF Bay PSR seeks to
rapidly advance policies and regulations in support of an equitable transition to all electric buildings. Switching
from fossil-fuel appliances to all electric appliances will help protect health and the planet.

| write to urge you to adopt the building electrification and decarbonizing strategy outlined in the report by
Rincon Consultants at your September 13 Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission meeting. It is essential
that the city consider all reasonable measures to prevent new uses of gas and facilitate the necessary transition
from fossil gas to address the air quality, health, and safety impacts of current fossil gas use in our homes and
other buildings. The framework provided by the report authors, Rincon Consultants, will provide a clear path for
every San Mateo homeowner, landlord, and commercial property owner to take the one most direct,
immediate step to stop the march of the climate crisis: Electrify Everything!

A rapid transition away from fossil fuel use is also critical to avoid the very worst and irreversible impacts of
climate change. Preventing the continued use of fossil fuels, including “natural gas” (which is primarily
methane, a gas that has 80 times the warming power of carbon dioxide), creates more affordable, cleaner,
healthier, and more resilient housing and buildings for communities.

While the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) report revealed that sadly, a 1.5°C rise in
planetary temperature is now unavoidable, the potential to limit warming to below 2°C—and avoid even more
catastrophic climate impacts—is still possible if the world can achieve net-zero carbon emissions by

2050.{i] That means we need to begin phasing out fossil fuels right away, including methane gas used to heat
and cook with.

1.Building electrification is a key strategy for addressing our climate emergency

241 of 332


--- page 242 ---
@ Greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions from California’s building sector account for more than a quarter of the
state’s total emissions. Direct emissions from building fossil fuel use account for 10— 15% of the total. These
emissions result primarily from both the combustion of gas in buildings for cooking, heating, and water heating
as well as from methane leaks throughout the gas distribution system.” (UCLA 2019 page 3).

e Building electrification (BE), defined as “replacing gas with efficient electric appliances in existing buildings
and constructing new building as all-electric” is the primary approach to building decarbonization.

@ Phasing out gas use provides many benefits to community health, safety, and a stable climate future.
Extending these benefits to existing homes and buildings is now urgently needed.

2.Building electrification prevents toxic exposures to air pollution from gas stoves and gas appliances. These are
some of the health effects of exposure to natural gas.

e California has the highest percentage of gas stove use in the country. 88% of all CA households (11.5 million in
total) having natural gas service in 2020; typically, 70% of these households cook with a natural gas stove or
oven,

e Natural gas throughout California contains numerous hazardous air pollutants that are linked to cancer,
asthma, and the formation of smog.

@ Scientists documented that even when gas stoves are off they can leak benzene (a known carcinogen) in
concentrations such that indoor air concentrations are on a par with secondhand smoke.

e Homes with gas stoves can emit nitrogen dioxide concentrations that are 50-400% higher than homes with
electric stoves. Nitrogen dioxide causes direct damage to people’s lungs and is one of the primary causes of
smog.

@ Children in homes with gas stoves have a 42% increased risk of experiencing asthma symptoms, a 24%
increased risk of ever being diagnosed with asthma by a doctor, and an overall 32% increased risk of both
current and lifetime asthma.

e Chronic exposure to elevated fine particulate matter (also known as PM2.5) has the potential to damage
human respiratory systems, the cardiovascular system, is harmful to pregnant women, and is one of the leading

causes of premature death throughout the world.

@ Improperly vented gas appliances lead to carbon monoxide poisoning that result in thousands of emergency
room visits and several hundred deaths every year

3. Pollution from gas stoves disproportionately harms children in communities of color

e African-American and Hispanic children with asthma are likely the most disproportionately burdened by
indoor air pollution from gas stoves.

e Poor people without adequate heating will often use gas stoves to heat their home which contributes to
indoor air pollution.

@ Lower-income and communities of color are three times more likely to live in an area with poor outdoor air

quality, which compounds indoor air pollution health harms.
2

242 of 332


--- page 243 ---
4.Other benefits of building electrification

e Electrifying our building stock produces a new demand for skilled workers. A 2019 UCLA study documented
(p. ES-4) that building electrification in California could support an average of 64,200-104, 100 jobs annually,
after accounting for losses in the gas industry. The greatest increases in employment would be building retrofits
and renewable energy construction, while the greatest decreases would be in gas distribution followed by
labor-saving all-electric new construction. However, the negative labor impacts are much smaller than the
positive impacts.

e All-Electric homes and buildings are more efficient. According to the California Energy Commission, a modern
high-efficiency heat pump electric water heater (available at all major retailers) costs roughly one-third less on
utility bills to operate than the most efficient gas water heater. in addition, electric heat pump heating also
provides air-conditioning, resulting in less equipment, reduced maintenance costs, and greater climate
resilience.

e Public Safety: Methane gas is highly flammable. In the past 10 years, 9,000 gas explosions in the U.S have
killed more than 500 people, and gas leaks have displaced and sickened thousands of people [iii] Methane gas
also caused half the fires after two major California earthquakes [ii]

e Climate: All-electric buildings are a practical step forward to address the climate crisis, by breaking the cycle
of fossil fuel dependency in buildings. This is the single biggest step that cities can take to address climate.

e Resilience: Switching from gas to electric at the time of remodel or replacement helps avoid a complex, costly
and likely inevitable switch to all-electric heating and appliances in the future, since gas prices are expected to
rise sharply, and California is planning to eventually end gas distribution. The California Public Utilities
Commission estimates that natural gas rates will increase at twice the rate of electricity through the next 10
years.|iv]

Thank you for considering our comments. We would be pleased to provide additional information or respond to
any questions that might arise.

Jeffrey A. Mann, M.D.

Lafayette, California

e Lower-income and communities of color are three times more likely to live in an area with poor
outdoor air quality, which compounds indoor air pollution health harms.

4.Other benefits of building electrification
@ Electrifying our building stock produces a new demand for skilled workers. A 2019 UCLA
study documented (p. ES-4) that building electrification in California could support an average of

64,200-104,100 jobs annually, after accounting for losses in the gas industry. The greatest increases in
employment would be building retrofits and renewable energy construction, while the greatest

246 of 332


--- page 247 ---
decreases would be in gas distribution followed by labor-saving all-electric new construction. However,
the negative labor impacts are much smaller than the positive impacts.

e All-Electric homes and buildings are more efficient. According to the California Energy Commission,
a modern high-efficiency heat pump electric water heater (available at all major retailers) costs roughly
one-third less on utility bills to operate than the most efficient gas water heater. In addition, electric
heat pump heating also provides air-conditioning, resulting in less equipment, reduced maintenance
costs, and greater climate resilience.

e Public Safety: Methane gas is highly flammable. In the past 10 years, 9,000 gas explosions in the U.S
have killed more than 500 people, and gas leaks have displaced and sickened thousands of

people. [iii] Methane gas also caused half the fires after two major California earthquakes. lii]

@ Climate: All-electric buildings are a practical step forward to address the climate crisis, by breaking the
cycle of fossil fuel dependency in buildings. This is the single biggest step that cities can take to address
climate.

e Resilience: Switching from gas to electric at the time of remodel or replacement helps avoid a
complex, costly and likely inevitable switch to all-electric heating and appliances in the future, since gas
prices are expected to rise sharply, and California is planning to eventually end gas distribution. The
California Public Utilities Commission estimates that natural gas rates will increase at twice the rate of

electricity through the next 10 years. |'V]

Thank you for considering our comments. We would be pleased to provide additional information or
respond to any questions that might arise.

Jeffrey A. Mann, M.D.

Lafayette, California

From: Guillermo Cockrum

Sent: Wednesday, September 13, 2023 1:40 PM
To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission
Subject: City Building De-Carbonization

Dear Sustainability & Infrastructure Commissioners,

| appreciate your leadership in the City of San Mateo's decarbonization efforts and the release of the draft
study for review. San Mateo's commitment to decarbonization is commendable.

| strongly support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the city's structures, primarily for health and financial
reasons:

» Local Health Impacts: Gas appliances pose identified health risks. The Bay Area Air Quality
Management District recently passed Rule 9-4 and 9-6 to eliminate future gas water heaters and
HVAC systems due to the health effects of nitrogen oxide and particulate matter. The staff report
estimates doing so would save up to 85 lives and 15,000 asthma attacks a year. Note, this is for
outdoor air. Indoor air is likely worse.

+» Regional/Global Health Impacts: Burning natural gas/methane contributes to a warming climate with
adverse effects on residents' lives, from extreme heat to more destructive wildfires. Extreme heat is
the leading weather cause of death. Climate change multiplies these threats.

» Environmental Concerns: Methane gas extraction methods like hydraulic fracturing harm our
environment and frontline communitie

« Cost Savings: Transitioning to electric will bring long-term cost savings, benefiting households by an
estimated $1,800 annually. As technologies advance, costs will further decrease.

+ Local Support: San Mateo benefits from local initiatives and incentives, making electrification
affordable and accessible

e Simplified Electrification: The grid is becoming more reliable, and new electric products reduce the
need for extensive rewiring. Streamlined processes and local workforce development support
electrification.

Denying the urgency of decarbonization ignores the reality of an unhealthy, hotter, costlier, and less
predictable future. Decarbonization aligns with both moral and financial considerations. With numerous
compelling reasons to accelerate electrification in San Mateo, | urge you to continue facilitating our progress.

Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to public welfare.

All the best,

Guillermo Cockrum

Dear Sustainability & Infrastructure Commissioners,

| appreciate your leadership in the City of San Mateo's decarbonization efforts and the release of the draft study for
review. San Mateo's commitment to decarbonization is commendable.

| strongly support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the city's structures, primarily for health and financial reasons
as outlined below:

Local Health Impacts: Gas appliances pose identified health risks. The Bay Area Air Quality Management District recently
passed Rule 9-4 and 9-6 to eliminate future gas water heaters and HVAC systems due to the health effects of nitrogen
oxide and particulate matter. The staff report estimates doing so would save up to 85 lives and 15,000 asthma attacks a
year. Note, this is for outdoor air. Indoor air is likely worse.

Regional/Global Health Impacts: Burning natural gas/methane contributes to a warming climate with adverse effects on
residents’ lives, from extreme heat to more destructive wildfires, Extreme heat is the leading weather cause of

death. Climate change multiplies these threats.

Environmental Concerns: Methane gas extraction methods like hydraulic fracturing harm our environment and frontline
communities.

Cost Savings: Transitioning to electric will bring long-term cost savings, benefiting households by an estimated $1,800
annually, As technologies advance, costs will further decrease.

Local Support: San Mateo benefits from local initiatives and incentives, making electrification affordable and accessible.
Simplified Electrification: The grid is becoming more reliable every day, and new electric products reduce the need for
extensive rewiring. Peninsula Clean Energy is streamlining processes and developing a one-stop shop to assist
homeowners with electrification (whole-home and partial). Community groups are working with unions and contractors
to develop the electrification workforce.

Denying the urgency of decarbonization ignores the reality of an unhealthy, hotter, costlier, and less predictable future.
Decarbonization aligns with both moral and financial considerations. With numerous compelling reasons to accelerate
electrification in San Mateo, | urge you to continue facilitating our progress.

Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to public welfare.

Sincerely,

Laura Brash

| thank San Mateo for being one of the only cities in the country to be taking the necessary steps to address

you have to stick to the commitments that the city has made to their constituents.

Some community members have raised concerns about the costs of electrification. The reality is that they have
come down substantially. Furthermore, as technologies begin to scale and markets grow, costs will continue
to come down and electrification will be cheaper in the long term, especially when we factor in the savings from
improvements to the climate and community health. We must be willing to be a pioneer and make that choice
to be uncomfortable with “pioneer status” in the short term to actually be able to live in the long term.

San Mateo is in a unique position to be that pioneer because of the resources the city has for PCE rebates,
IRA tax credits, and the social infrastructure to educate people about the process of electrification and how to
make it as easy as possible. Even the consultants from the city conceded that electrification is less expensive
when considering rebates.

The urgency of the climate crisis can not be overstated. Please listen to the youth. Our future is in your hands.

Anjuli Mishra

Dear Sustainability and Infrastructure Commissioners:

Thank you and City staff for releasing the draft study in response to the City Council's approved objective for
FY 23-24: “Establish policies to decarbonize and electrify existing buildings and eliminate natural gas use by
2030.”

| would also like to urge you to continue the forward momentum on this process. We need to keep supporting
decarbonization —through all means possible, but specifically, by focusing on building electrification.

Building electrification is one of the most important responses to the climate crisis. The framework provided by
the report authors, Rincon Consultants, will provide a clear path for every San Mateo homeowner, landlord,
and commercial property owner to take the one most direct, immediate step to stop the march of the climate
crisis: Electrify Everything! Stop burning fossil fuels including methane gas.

According to Electrify Now (https://electrifynow.net/), every home that is electrified eliminates 9 -19 tons of
global warming carbon dioxide emissions, every single year. That is on top of the 4 tons of CO2 emissions per
year per home that are saved by signing on to Peninsula Clean Energy.

Regarding cost of electrification, Rincon Consultants notes on page 18 in the report, that: “Whole home
electrification could be less expensive for owners in San Mateo than replacing appliances with gas
once rebates are included.”

| strongly urge the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission to continue to support and promote the City
Council objective to decarbonize buildings and end the use of gas in San Mateo.

Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to our city.

Nancy Schneider

To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject: San Mateo - Appliance Conversion from Gas to Electric (Electrify San Mateo)

Dear Commission and Council Members.

I am unable to join the meeting in person tonight. I'm concerned that an unpublicized
recommendation will be made to move some of the mandates forward to 2025, from
2030 and want to ask you to consider declining the fast-track Appliance Conversion from
Gas to Electric initiative, should it come up.

Keep in mind that a conversion such as this is costly for all of us, not just the cost of a
new appliance. Consider that within our home, to convert from gas to electric could
mean bearing the additional cost of running new electrical wiring, possibly requiring
upgraded and/or new electrical panels, potentially modifying existing locations for
appliances to fit, etc. Should all this be done within this accelerated program to 2025
from 2030, are resources available to accommodate the demand (ie: materials, general
contractors & electricans). Have you verified that PG&E even has increased their
capacity availability (some think there would be an inability for PGE to provide the
electrical services although I have not verified this myself)? Would a new substation(s)
be required and where will they be placed? Have you also considered that upgrading
existing homes/ offices will increase the monthly cost of rentals, affecting more
businesses and residents. Further, I understand that there may be a rebate but for
many, even if they qualify based on usage (a single person using minimal gas, such as
myself would not even qualify), however it would not cover the cost of the onerous
burden you would unnecessarily mandate.

While I appreciate we must look at options for curbing climate change and reducing the
carbon foot-print, it seems to me that we should also do so in a thoughtful, cost-
effective manner.

Many are struggling to meet financial obligations in these economic troubling times and
this initiative just does not help San Mateo. Since the proposed requirement to end gas
for EXISTING homes and buildings is above code set by the State of California AND it
would negatively impact residents, I request that you decline the plan, should it be
proposed at today's meeting.

Thank you for your consideration.

Sandra Jamme

From: Anna Cwirko-Godycki eet 9:i7
Sent: Wednesday, September T3,

To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Subject: Electric homes and Bike Lanes for San Mateo

Dear Commissioners:

ELECTRIC HOMES - great idea for the environment, but many reasons to delay implementation
from January 2025 to at least 2030. A city can also set realistic expectations for the number of
home conversions each year.

Reasons to delay:

1. Not clear on the specific details of the mandate.

2. Not clear on whether energy bills will be higher or lower. There is lots of debate and no clear
answer. Some studies suggest that expenditures will 2 or 3 times higher. Water heaters consume
45%-50% of energy needs for the home.

3. Not clear on whether the electric grid is sufficient for all those who will be tied to the grid.

2. San Mateo has citizens with various incomes, savings, financial resources.

Unless this mandate is economically feasible to property and business owners it should not be a
requirement. This mandate is itimidating and overwhelming. It will create undue hardship for
many families, especially retirees on fixed incomes. Yes, there are rebates and interest free loans,
but these must be clear to everyone, and a guarantee should be provided that if thousands of
homes will be upgraded at the same time there will be sufficient funds and contractors. We heard
that some people who converted their homes were unable to secure the rebates promised.

3. Is there a feasibility study on availability of sufficient professionals to prepare the electric home?
4. Is there a study on supply chain and availability of electric appliances?

5. Will the electric home require additional maintenance?

Such a major shift should not be a requirement in 1.5 years. A long period of public education and
preparation is needed.

People need to know precisely what rebates and loans are available and the processes to obtain
these. Non English speakers should have assistance with the paperwork.

BIKE LANES
While in theory | support the creation of bike lanes, | do not support them without careful
consideration of the needs of the entire community, not just the bikers.

Reasons to delay:
1. Displacing parking places for residents, resulting in parking on lawns is unconscionable.

2. Let's be real. San Mateo is not Copenhagen or Oslo in number of cyclists.
1

261 of 332


--- page 262 ---
3. Streets must be created with sidewalks, a lane for parking, a lane for bikes, and a lane for
traffic.

4, Building bike lanes on current streets, such as Norfolk will create traffic jams. There are already
traffic jams during high traffic periods (school drop off and pick up; entrance to 101 in the AM and
PM).

5. Only a minority of residents use bike lanes

6. Bike lanes are often improperly designed, give, provide a false sense of security and are often
dangerous to cars, bikers, and pedestrians.

Thank you for listening.

Anna Cwirko-Godycki

rower, Laure riecrer

Sent: Wednesday, September 13, 2023 3:24 PM
To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject: Electrification

Dear Sustainability and Infrastructure Commissioners:

Please do not accelerate the timeline for replacing gas appliances with electric appliances. The costs and timeframe for
replacements are too great for most people. As for indoor health, I've had a gas stove my whole life and no one in my
family has asthma. This is my choice. | do not want any of you to make that choice for me.

The City Council voted for the electrification ordinances over the objections of many:

* In 2020, the City Council adopted an ordinance requiring all residential and office buildings be all-electric
starting on January 1, 2021.

* In 2022, the City Council approved an ordinance that expanded the all-electric requirement to all new
buildings and requires electric-readiness and electric appliances for specific home remodels as of January
1, 2023.

In May 2023, the Bay Area Air Quality Management District (BAAQMD) adopted zero nitrogen oxides (NOx) standards
that will prohibit the sale and installation of gas water heaters starting in 2027 and gas furnaces in 2029 in the nine-
county Bay Area, These standards are the most ambitious in the country and outpace the state’s goal of banning the sale
of new gas furnaces and water heaters throughout the state Starting in 2030. There is no need for the City of San Mateo
to jump ahead in the timelines.

The state did an extensive analysis of costs and benefits before setting dates. What data has the City or Commission
analyzed that led you to believe accelerating time frames is appropriate, necessary, or will make any difference
regarding the world climate?

This requirement is an unnecessary burden on seniors and the disadvantaged community. Please do not accelerate any
timeline for electrification.

The push for electrification is premature. The state power availability is decreasing with the planned shutdown of two
nuclear plants. The transmission grid is aging and the lack of project upgrades proposed by PG&E

(see https://www.cpuc.ca.gov/industries-and-topics/electrical-energy/infrastructure/permittin -and-environmental-
review/current-project) make me question how we can avoid regular power outages.

Electrification takes control away from citizens. Electric power can be shut off much easier than shutting off natural gas.
| do not want to be cold and hungry when we have power outages that are all too frequent in California.

The highest equity priorities for San Mateo to focus on included prevention of evictions, support for homelessness, and
more education and

programmatic support for low-income residents. Electrification will unduly burden the community the city is trying to
protect.

Do not accelerate or expand electrification.

Thank you,

Sent: Wednesday, —_— = -_ 3:38 PM
To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Subject: Agenda Item #3 - "Electrify San Mateo — Building for the Future: City of San Mateo
Sustainable Buildings Strategy."

Dear Chair Rowinski, Commissioners, Staff, and Consultants,

Thank you for your continued progress towards decarbonizing the City of San Mateo’s building stock. The City
has proven to be a leader in this arena at a time when such a role is critical.

As we know, the burning of fossil fuels, including gas in our homes and buildings, is a major contributor to
global warming, the negative effects of which are impacting us with increased frequency and severity, both
locally and globally.

| am the father of a 9-year-old daughter. | am doing what | can to ensure a climate safe future for her and
others. We all, within our own individual and collective capacities, can play a role in creating a safe future for all
to thrive. A safe future is in serious jeopardy unless we transition away from burning fossil fuels to clean energy
and electrification as quickly as is humanly possible. The benefits of doing so go well beyond climate stability
and include substantially greater efficiency, lower energy costs, better air quality both indoors and out,
increased safety, greater equity, and stronger resilience. The decisions we make and the actions we take
today, will determine the livability of our planet for our children and future generations. We owe it to them to
make every effort possible to create a climate safe future.

Every fraction of a degree of warming that we can avoid matters. We are at a point in time when we no longer
have the luxury of moving slowly in the right direction, we must quicken the pace of our transition away from
fossil fuels. Let's show our children that we fully understand the magnitude of the climate crisis and that we will
act accordingly with courage, creativity, and conviction.

The technology to tackle most every building electrification situation is proven and readily available. As our grid
is becoming more renewable and more reliable, we must move in parallel to transition to electric devices that
can utilize this clean energy. The local electrification workforce is growing and proving to be up to the task, and
will continue to expand. Agencies such as Peninsula Clean Energy, companies such as QuitCarbon, and
multiple community organizations are providing building owners with assistance to simplify electrification.

For so many good reasons, let's keep up the momentum towards decarbonization and accelerate towards a
safer future by treating the climate crisis with the urgency that it demands and deserves. We have a moral
obligation to our children and future generations.

Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to public welfare.

Sincerely,

John McKenna

Subject: Electrification 2025 Reach Code - Opposition

Dear SIC Commissioners - I’m writing in opposition to fast-tracking electrification in San Mateo to 2025. Many of us with
good reason have very serious doubts about rushing the timelines for electrification, given PG&E's demonstrated
ineptitude, and inability to support existing demand much less a significant increase in demand. Likewise, there are
significant costs to property owners for conversion if forced. This should be more of a carrot (incentive-based) than stick
approach, and should not be rushed to this extent.

Thanks - Michael Weinhauer

| am very concerned to hear about the Proposal of the San Mateo Sustainability Committee (a non-elected body) that is
supported by the San Mateo City Council, namely, that it wishes to mandate that San Mateo residential property owners
convert their houses to all electric beginning January 2025.

This is an outrage for a number of reasons.

First, in a capitalist economy, | am able to choose how | want to spend the money that | earn. Why are you preventing
me from doing so? Why are you so afraid to let people choose their cars, appliances, home heating, and other items?
Why should you control me? Why do you insist on an artificial economy that no one wants?

Second, this is extremely expensive -- an estimate, including rewiring and new electrical boxes, will approximate
$100,000 for the average house. Please don't tell me that the "Inflation Reduction Act" will pay for it. The US is nearly
bankrupt now. (Inflation, you apparently do not know, is caused by too much money being injected into an economy --
too many dollars chasing too few goods. The "Inflation Reduction Act" is only adding to inflation, which is another tax on

everyone.)

Third, this will do nothing to help the "climate crisis."

Climate change is a hoax,

Last month, more than 1600 scientists, including two Nobel physics laureates, signed a declaration saying that there is
no climate emergency. An entire revamp of society is being planned without debate and without scientific evidence.

John Clauser, a Nobe Prize winning physicist disavows the climate "crisis."

A scientist who recently published in Nature acknowledged that he had to change his theory and narrow his focus,
disregarding all mitigating factors, in order to be published because of the pro-climate change bias at that journal.

| attended a very interesting talk in 2019 by a Stanford physics professor who applied chaos theory to the weather
patterns. Although climate change models have been unable to replicate historical temperatures of the past 100 years,
the professor was able to do so by his model without regard for carbon or "climate change."

A recent article (last week) by a Noble Prize-winning physicist points out that none of the climate change models (which

are unable to replicate historical temperatures of the past century) take clouds into account even though clouds can
change temperatures by 200% or more, far more than carbon is postulated to do. (Carbon influence is only a theory.)

But, of course, none of these individuals are as smart or knowledgeable as Adam Lorraine and Amarance Lee.

There is no evidence of climate having changed in San Mateo (or California).

overload the grid, putting millions of Californians at risk.

rrom,
Sent:
To:
Subject:

Kristin Hansen

Wednesday, rere

Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Public Comment Re: SIC Agenda Item 3 - Sustainable Buildings Strategy

Sustainability & Infrastructure Commissioners,

| appreciate your leadership in the City of San Mateo's decarbonization efforts and the release
of the draft study for review. San Mateo's commitment to decarbonization is commendable.

| strongly support eliminating fossil fuel appliances from the city's structures, primarily for

health and financial reasons:

Local Health Impacts: Gas appliances pose identified health risks. The Bay Area Air Quality
Management District recently passed Rule 9-4 and 9-6 to eliminate future gas water heaters
and HVAC systems due to the health effects of nitrogen oxide and particulate matter. The staff
report estimates doing so would save up to 85 lives and 15,000 asthma attacks a year. Note,

this is for outdoor air. indoor air is likely worse.

Regional/Global Health Impacts: Burning natural gas/methane contributes to a warming
climate with adverse effects on residents' lives, from extreme heat to more destructive
wildfires. Extreme heat is the leading weather cause of death. Climate change multiplies these

threats.

Environmental Concerns: Methane gas extraction methods like hydraulic fracturing harm our

environment and frontline communities.

Cost Savings: Transitioning to electric will bring long-term cost savings, benefiting households
by an estimated $1,800 annually. As technologies advance, costs will further decrease.

Local Support: San Mateo benefits from local initiatives and incentives, making electrification

affordable and accessible.

Simplified Electrification: The grid is becoming more reliable, and new electric products reduce
the need for extensive rewiring. Streamlined processes and local workforce development

support electrification.

273 of 332


--- page 274 ---

and less predictable future. Decarbonization aligns with both moral and financial
considerations. With numerous compelling reasons to accelerate electrification in San Mateo,

| urge you to continue facilitating our progress.
Thank you for your dedicated service and commitment to public welfare.

Sincerely,

Kristin Hansen

May | offer to you my perspective on the positive impacts that electrification have:

As a youth in today’s society, the climate crisis sits on the forefront of my consciousness. This concern is also shared by
many others in my generation. Knowing that San Mateo county is actively promoting electrification helps alleviate these
concerns for me and my peers.

The switch to electric cooking appliances will benefit those with respiratory illnesses. | have seen firsthand the benefits
of this switch. My sister, who suffers from asthma, sees more days without respiratory attacks as a result of our
installment of an electric stove.

Electrification of our city will not only clean up the air in our homes and help us secure the health of current and future
generations, but it will also reduce our city’s carbon footprint and create jobs that myself and other youth will occupy in
the coming years.

| would like to assure you that the work of the Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission to electrify the county has the
support of the Youth, those that suffer from respiratory illness like my sister, and those that are concerned for the state

of our climate. May the Sustainable Buildings Strategy project help San Mateo set a precedent for other cities to follow
and bring the benefits of electrification to countless other communities.

Thank you.

▪Reach Climate Action Plan Goals:
▪BE-2: All-electric existing buildings
▪2030: Reduce emissions 40% below 1990 levels
▪Building emissions make up 38% of the City total
▪Gas accounts for (85)% of building related 
emissions
▪Electrification of existing buildings is the 
most cost-effective way to achieve carbon-
free buildings
▪Electricity will be carbon free by 2045 (SB 
100)- San Mateo is already on the way with 
ECO100 from Peninsula Clean Energy
▪Any replacement of new gas appliances locks in 
fossil fuel infrastructure, taking us farther from 
achieving climate goals
▪Building electrification can achieve a host of 
other co-benefits, including indoor air quality, 
protection from rising gas prices, and 
concurrent building upgrades

What is existing building electrification?  
• Switching from using natural gas to 
carbon-free electricity for heating/ 
cooling, cooking, and clothes drying 
in our homes, apartments, 
offices, stores, and beyond.
• Why? Allows the City of 
San Mateo to achieve climate 
goals while increasing 
community health, 
affordability, and resiliency 
through upgraded buildings 
and appliances
Image source: SCE
284 of 332

--- page 285 ---
How do we electrify 
buildings? 
▪Building Electrification: Appliances that use gas are replaced with 
electric technologies
▪‘Electrify on Replacement’ & Cost Effectiveness: Replacing gas 
appliances with electric when they stop working (‘burnout’), or 
would have been upgraded anyway, increases cost effectiveness 
since appliance would have been replaced regardless. Cost 
of electric technologies are supported by incentives from PCE, 
IRA, BayREN, and TECH.
Space heating and 
cooling: Gas Furnace →
Heat Pump
Water heating: 
Gas water heater →Heat Pump 
Hot Water Heater
Cooking: 
Gas stove →Induction Stove
Clothes Drying:
Gas Clothes Drying →
Electric Dryer

•
Gas bills could more than double over time
▪Resilience & Safety 
•
Decreased fire & carbon monoxide risk, increased resilience with 
solar
▪Equity 
•
Equitable access to health, safety, upgraded buildings & comfort 
benefits.

Local Policy Context: City of San Mateo Building Electrification (Reach 
Codes)

permit is issued:
• Single family homes + multifamily: panel 
capacity;
• Single family homes and duplexes: outlets 
installed; kitchen + laundry renovation
•
Single family homes and duplexes: Installation 
of heat pump air conditioning when air con is 
installed or replaced

extension of fuel gas for new fireplaces; firepits; 
grills; pools
• Single family homes and duplexes: requires 
HPWH installation during addition + alteration
▪New Construction: Started Jan. 1, 2023

and 6 
▪NOx water heaters phased out by 2027 
▪NOx furnaces by 2029

Water Heaters are currently the only Zero 
NOx option. 
Most stringent building decarbonization

the opportunity to be ahead of the curve 
for compliance by taking action early

Equity + Analysis = Policy Analysis Framework
▪Your feedback will be critical in refining

▪Equity Criteria informs direction for 
how to equitably electrify existing 
residential and commercial buildings; 
▪Effectiveness criteria ensures full

and that there will be no unintended 
consequences to other City priorities,

owners
▪Each policy pathway should include

Energy Equity Definition 
The concept of Energy Equity recognizes that 
disadvantaged communities have been 
historically marginalized and overburdened by 
pollution, underinvestment in clean energy 
infrastructure, and lack of access to energy 
efficient housing and transportation 
(Department of Energy, Office of Energy Efficiency and Renewable Energy). https://www.energy.gov/eere/energy-equity-and-
environmental-justice

Electrification implications + Key Takeaways
▪~96,800 single family residential buildings
▪70% of City building stock was built in 1970 
or earlier
▪Before 1970, panel and service upgrades 
could be more common
▪Buildings built before 1970 are more likely 
to have electric panels of 100 amps or less, 
or fuse boxes, both of which may present 
hurdles to electrify
▪However, retrofit ready heat pump 
products, circuit sharing technologies, and 
home electrification plans could help 
building owners avoid panel and service 
upgrades

--- page 320 ---
Overview: Residential Cost Analysis 
Framework
▪Rincon analyzed upfront costs 
to electrify based on available 
data from PCE, BayREN, and the 
County of San Mateo
▪Upfront costs = appliance + 
install labor + associated costs 
like permits and wiring
▪Panel upgrades were broken 
out as a separate cost
This Photo by Unknown Author is licensed under CC BY
320 of 332

--- page 321 ---
Key Takeaways: Upfront Residential Electrification Costs
Marginal costs for electrification are higher, but 
can reach parity with existing rebates.
Whole home electrification could save San Mateans $709 
when compared to the cost of gas-for-gas appliance 
replacements.
• Full-home appliance replacement with new gas
appliances: $11,012 - $18,512
• Marginal cost of full-home electrification before
rebates: $13,291- $20,936
• Marginal cost of full-home electrification after
rebates: +$4,836 to -$709 (cost savings)

+TECH Total Electric Home Rebates (all systems): $5,500
PCE also provides up to $10,000 in zero percent loans for building electrification. 
*As of August 28 2023; Incentives change regularly based on stacking; availability. These incentives will be updated prior to community outreach

Gas-For-Gas Scenario
Electrification implications + Key 
Takeaways
▪Most San Mateans (75%) do not have AC 
▪If a building owner were to replace 
every electrifiable appliance, with a 
similar gas appliance, they would spend 
$11,012 w/o AC
▪Key takeaway: building owners would 
have invested in costly appliance 
upgrades regardless, in a ‘electrify on 
replacement’ scenario

Gas-to-Electric Scenario
No Incentives
Electrification implications + Key Takeaways
▪Avoiding panel upgrades through home 
electrification planning, panel splitters, “watt 
diet” etc. could save building owners ~$3,700
▪Because of significant market, labor quote 
variation in HVAC system, Rincon ran two cost 
scenarios to control for significant variation 
(low, median cost) 
▪Total cost to electrify without incentives: 
$24,303-$31,948

327 of 332

--- page 328 ---
Commercial Building Cost Analysis
▪Costs are highly variable, most large buildings have over sized systems, preventing a 1:1 replacement without 
efficiency or downsizing measure first 
▪Small and medium sized retail or service buildings have similar electrification costs to single-family homes. 
▪Most interviewers recommend building performance standards, as electrifying large buildings cannot be a ‘one-
size-fits-all’ approach
▪Rooftop package units offer relative cost parity in comparison to gas, even without additional incentive
▪Potential cost-effective policy lever 
Data sources: Rincon contractor interviews (City of Sacramento), Rocky Mountain Institute Economics of Electrifying Existing 
Buildings, PCE 2035 Decarbonization Plan 
PCE 2035 Decarbonization Plan shows near 
cost parity for rooftop packaged heat pump 
installation costs
